The plant can supply electrical energy for approximately 19.95 hours using the energy stored in the molten salt.


---

<a id='oppgave72'></a>

# Question 72: Lyskæde

## Question Images

![Question 72 Image](images/oppgave72_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_108.jpg)

![Question 72 Image](images/oppgave72_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_107.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


Determine the resistance of a single bulb in a series of 14 identical bulbs connected to a 230 V supply, where each bulb dissipates 2.7 W.

#### Key Concepts

- **Ohm's Law**: Relates voltage ($V$), current ($I$), and resistance ($R$) as $V = IR$.
- **Power Formula**: Power ($P$) is related to voltage and current by $P = VI$.

#### Formulas Used

1. Power formula: 
   

$$P = VI$$


   This formula relates the power dissipated by a device to the voltage across it and the current through it.

2. Ohm's Law:
   

$$V = IR$$


   This formula relates the voltage across a resistor to the current through it and its resistance.

#### Step-by-Step Solution

1. Calculate the total current through the series circuit using the power formula:
   

$$P = VI \implies I = \frac{P}{V}$$


   For one bulb, $P = 2.7 \text{ W}$ and $V = \frac{230 \text{ V}}{14}$ (since the voltage is equally divided among 14 bulbs).

2. Calculate the voltage across one bulb:
   

$$V_{bulb} = \frac{230 \text{ V}}{14}$$



3. Calculate the current through one bulb:
   

$$I = \frac{2.7 \text{ W}}{V_{bulb}}$$



4. Use Ohm's Law to find the resistance of one bulb:
   

$$R = \frac{V_{bulb}}{I}$$



#### Final Answer

The resistance of one bulb is approximately 1180 Ω.

### Part B


Determine the power dissipated in one intact bulb when one bulb's filament is burnt out and the current passes through a shunt with a voltage drop of 31 V.

#### Key Concepts

- **Series Circuit**: In a series circuit, the total voltage is the sum of the voltages across each component.
- **Power Dissipation**: Power dissipated in a resistor is given by $P = I^2R$ or $P = VI$.

#### Formulas Used

1. Ohm's Law:
   

$$V = IR$$


   This formula relates the voltage across a resistor to the current through it and its resistance.

2. Power formula:
   

$$P = VI$$


   This formula relates the power dissipated by a device to the voltage across it and the current through it.

#### Step-by-Step Solution

1. Calculate the total voltage across the remaining bulbs and shunt:
   

$$V_{total} = 230 \text{ V} - 31 \text{ V} = 199 \text{ V}$$



2. Calculate the current through the circuit using the resistance of one bulb (from part a):
   

$$I = \frac{V_{total}}{R_{total}}$$


   where $R_{total} = 13 \times R_{bulb}$.

3. Calculate the power dissipated in one bulb:
   

$$P_{bulb} = I^2 \times R_{bulb}$$



#### Final Answer

The power dissipated in one intact bulb is approximately 2.4 W.

---

<a id='oppgave73'></a>

# Question 73: 75Se til undersøgelse af kroppens galdesystem

## Question Images

![Question 73 Image](images/oppgave73_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_109.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
Determine the nuclear reaction for the formation of $^{75}$Se from $^{75}$As by proton bombardment.

#### Key Concepts
- **Nuclear Reactions**: Involves the transformation of one element into another by changing the number of protons and neutrons.
- **Proton Bombardment**: A process where protons are used to induce nuclear reactions.

#### Formulas Used
- **Nuclear Reaction Equation**: 
  

$$ ^A_ZX + ^1_1p \rightarrow ^{A+1}_{Z+1}Y + ^0_1n $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the Initial and Final Nuclei**:
   - Initial nucleus: $^{75}$As (Arsenic)
   - Final nucleus: $^{75}$Se (Selenium)
   
2. **Write the Reaction**:
   - Bombard $^{75}$As with a proton ($^1_1p$):
   

$$ ^{75}_{33}As + ^1_1p \rightarrow ^{75}_{34}Se + ^0_1n $$


   
3. **Check Conservation**:
   - Mass number: $75 + 1 = 76$, $75 + 1 = 76$
   - Atomic number: $33 + 1 = 34$, $34$

#### Final Answer
The nuclear reaction is: 


$$ ^{75}_{33}As + ^1_1p \rightarrow ^{75}_{34}Se + ^0_1n $$



### Part B

#### Problem Summary
Determine the biological half-life of $^{75}$Se in SeHCAT given the decay data.

#### Key Concepts
- **Biological Half-Life**: The time it takes for half of a substance to be eliminated from a biological system.
- **Decay Formula**: Relates the initial and final activity with time and decay constant.

#### Formulas Used
- **Decay Formula**: 
  

$$ N(t) = N_0 e^{-\lambda t} $$


- **Half-life Formula**: 
  

$$ T_{1/2} = \frac{\ln(2)}{\lambda} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Initial and Final Activity**:
   - Initial activity $N_0 = 5.80 \times 10^4$ decays/min
   - Final activity $N(t) = 0.701 \times 10^4$ decays/min
   - Time $t = 7.00$ days = $7.00 \times 24 \times 60$ minutes

2. **Use Decay Formula**:
   

$$ 0.701 \times 10^4 = 5.80 \times 10^4 e^{-\lambda (7.00 \times 24 \times 60)} $$



3. **Solve for $\lambda$**:
   

$$ \frac{0.701}{5.80} = e^{-\lambda (7.00 \times 24 \times 60)} $$


   

$$ \ln\left(\frac{0.701}{5.80}\right) = -\lambda (7.00 \times 24 \times 60) $$


   

$$ \lambda = -\frac{\ln\left(\frac{0.701}{5.80}\right)}{7.00 \times 24 \times 60} $$



4. **Calculate Biological Half-Life**:
   

$$ T_{1/2} = \frac{\ln(2)}{\lambda} $$



#### Final Answer
The biological half-life of $^{75}$Se in SeHCAT is approximately calculated using the above steps.

### Part C

#### Problem Summary
Calculate the equivalent dose received by a person standing 3.1 m away from a source for 45 minutes.

#### Key Concepts
- **Equivalent Dose**: A measure of the biological effect of radiation, considering the type of radiation.
- **Gamma Factor**: Used to calculate dose from activity.

#### Formulas Used
- **Dose Rate Formula**: 
  

$$ \text{Dose Rate} = \frac{\text{Activity} \times \text{Gamma Factor}}{\text{Distance}^2} $$


- **Total Dose**: 
  

$$ \text{Total Dose} = \text{Dose Rate} \times \text{Time} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Given Data**:
   - Activity $A = 3.70$ MBq
   - Gamma factor = $0.23 \frac{\text{mSv} \cdot \text{m}^2}{\text{h} \cdot \text{GBq}}$
   - Distance $d = 3.1$ m
   - Time $t = 45$ minutes = $0.75$ hours

2. **Convert Activity to GBq**:
   

$$ A = 3.70 \text{ MBq} = 0.00370 \text{ GBq} $$



3. **Calculate Dose Rate**:
   

$$ \text{Dose Rate} = \frac{0.00370 \times 0.23}{3.1^2} \text{ mSv/h} $$



4. **Calculate Total Dose**:
   

$$ \text{Total Dose} = \text{Dose Rate} \times 0.75 \text{ h} $$



#### Final Answer
The equivalent dose received by the person is calculated using the above steps.

---

<a id='oppgave74'></a>

# Question 74: Sikkerhedsnet til klipper

## Question Images

![Question 74 Image](images/oppgave74_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_110.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
A concrete block falls freely from a height of 42 meters. We need to determine the time it takes for the block to reach the safety net.

#### Key Concepts
- **Free Fall:** An object in free fall is only under the influence of gravity.
- **Acceleration due to Gravity (g):** The acceleration of an object due to Earth's gravity is approximately 9.81 m/s².

#### Formulas Used
- The formula for the time of free fall is derived from the equation of motion:
  

$$ s = \frac{1}{2} g t^2 $$


  where:
  - $s$ is the distance fallen (42 m),
  - $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity (9.81 m/s²),
  - $t$ is the time in seconds.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Rearrange the equation to solve for $t$:
   

$$ t = \sqrt{\frac{2s}{g}} $$


2. Substitute the given values:
   

$$ t = \sqrt{\frac{2 \times 42}{9.81}} $$


3. Calculate:
   

$$ t = \sqrt{\frac{84}{9.81}} $$


   

$$ t = \sqrt{8.56} $$


   

$$ t \approx 2.93 \text{ seconds} $$



#### Final Answer
The time it takes for the concrete block to fall to the safety net is approximately 2.93 seconds.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary
When the concrete block hits the safety net, it stretches the net by 8.15 meters. We need to determine the spring constant of the net.

#### Key Concepts
- **Hooke's Law:** The force exerted by a spring is proportional to its extension or compression.
- **Energy Conservation:** The potential energy lost by the block is converted into elastic potential energy in the net.

#### Formulas Used
- **Potential Energy (PE):**
  

$$ PE = mgh $$


  where:
  - $m$ is the mass (25,000 kg),
  - $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity (9.81 m/s²),
  - $h$ is the height (42 m).
- **Elastic Potential Energy (EPE):**
  

$$ EPE = \frac{1}{2} k x^2 $$


  where:
  - $k$ is the spring constant,
  - $x$ is the extension (8.15 m).

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Calculate the potential energy lost:
   

$$ PE = 25000 \times 9.81 \times 42 $$


   

$$ PE = 10,297,500 \text{ J} $$


2. Set the potential energy equal to the elastic potential energy:
   

$$ 10,297,500 = \frac{1}{2} k (8.15)^2 $$


3. Solve for $k$:
   

$$ k = \frac{2 \times 10,297,500}{(8.15)^2} $$


   

$$ k = \frac{20,595,000}{66.4225} $$


   

$$ k \approx 310,080 \text{ N/m} $$



#### Final Answer
The spring constant of the safety net is approximately 310,080 N/m.

---

<a id='oppgave75'></a>

# Question 75: Tiangong 1

## Question Images

![Question 75 Image](images/oppgave75_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_112.jpg)

![Question 75 Image](images/oppgave75_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_111.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
Determine the gravitational force on the Tiangong 1 space station in its orbit.

#### Key Concepts
- **Gravitational Force**: The force between two masses is given by Newton's law of universal gravitation.

#### Formulas Used
- Gravitational Force: 
  

$$ F = \frac{G \cdot m_1 \cdot m_2}{r^2} $$


  where:
  - $G$ is the gravitational constant, $6.674 \times 10^{-11} \, \text{m}^3\,\text{kg}^{-1}\,\text{s}^{-2}$.
  - $m_1$ and $m_2$ are the masses of the two objects.
  - $r$ is the distance between the centers of the two masses.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the masses**:
   - Mass of Earth, $m_1 = 5.972 \times 10^{24} \, \text{kg}$.
   - Mass of Tiangong 1, $m_2 = 8506 \, \text{kg}$.

2. **Calculate the distance $r$**:
   - Radius of Earth = $6371 \, \text{km}$.
   - Height of orbit = $352 \, \text{km}$.
   - Total distance $r = 6371 + 352 = 6723 \, \text{km} = 6723000 \, \text{m}$.

3. **Calculate the gravitational force**:
   

$$ F = \frac{6.674 \times 10^{-11} \cdot 5.972 \times 10^{24} \cdot 8506}{(6723000)^2} $$


   

$$ F \approx 7.34 \times 10^4 \, \text{N} $$



#### Final Answer
The gravitational force on Tiangong 1 is approximately $7.34 \times 10^4 \, \text{N}$.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary
Calculate the power exerted by air resistance on Tiangong 1 in its orbit.

#### Key Concepts
- **Power**: The rate at which work is done or energy is transferred.
- **Work done by a force**: Work is the product of force and the distance over which it acts.

#### Formulas Used
- Power: 
  

$$ P = F \cdot v $$


  where:
  - $P$ is the power.
  - $F$ is the force.
  - $v$ is the velocity.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the force**:
   - Air resistance force, $F = 9.4 \, \text{mN} = 9.4 \times 10^{-3} \, \text{N}$.

2. **Calculate the orbital velocity**:
   - Use the formula for circular orbital velocity:
   

$$ v = \sqrt{\frac{G \cdot M}{r}} $$


   - $M$ is the mass of Earth, $5.972 \times 10^{24} \, \text{kg}$.
   - $r = 6723000 \, \text{m}$ (as calculated in part a).
   

$$ v = \sqrt{\frac{6.674 \times 10^{-11} \cdot 5.972 \times 10^{24}}{6723000}} $$


   

$$ v \approx 7700 \, \text{m/s} $$



3. **Calculate the power**:
   

$$ P = 9.4 \times 10^{-3} \cdot 7700 $$


   

$$ P \approx 72.38 \, \text{W} $$



#### Final Answer
The power exerted by air resistance on Tiangong 1 is approximately $72.38 \, \text{W}$.

### Part C

#### Problem Summary
Determine the decrease in altitude per orbit for Tiangong 1 on March 20, 2018.

#### Key Concepts
- **Orbital Decay**: The gradual decrease in the altitude of a satellite's orbit due to atmospheric drag.

#### Formulas Used
- None specific; use graphical analysis and data interpretation.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Analyze the graph**:
   - The graph shows the altitude of Tiangong 1 from March 1 to April 1.
   - On March 20, the altitude is approximately 250 km.
   - By April 1, the altitude is near 0 km.

2. **Estimate the number of orbits per day**:
   - Orbital period $T$ can be estimated using:
   

$$ T = \frac{2\pi r}{v} $$


   - $r = 6723000 \, \text{m}$, $v = 7700 \, \text{m/s}$ (as calculated in part b).
   

$$ T \approx \frac{2\pi \times 6723000}{7700} \approx 5400 \, \text{s} \approx 90 \, \text{min} $$


   - Approximately 16 orbits per day.

3. **Calculate the altitude decrease per orbit**:
   - Total altitude decrease from March 20 to April 1 is approximately 250 km.
   - Number of days = 12.
   - Total orbits = $16 \times 12 = 192$.
   - Altitude decrease per orbit = $\frac{250}{192} \approx 1.3 \, \text{km/orbit}$.

#### Final Answer
The altitude of Tiangong 1 decreased by approximately $1.3 \, \text{km}$ per orbit on March 20, 2018.

---

<a id='oppgave76'></a>

# Question 76: Gotthard togstrækningen

## Question Images

![Question 76 Image](images/oppgave76_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_113.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Calculate the potential energy required to move a fully loaded freight train from Airolo (211 m above sea level) to the highest point (1151 m above sea level).

#### Key Concepts
- **Potential Energy (PE):** The energy possessed by an object due to its position relative to a reference point, typically calculated as $PE = mgh$.

#### Formulas Used
- **Potential Energy Formula:**
  

$$PE = mgh$$


  - **m:** mass of the object (in kg)
  - **g:** acceleration due to gravity (9.81 m/s²)
  - **h:** height difference (in meters)

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Mass of the train, $m = 1.53 \times 10^6$ kg
   - Height at Airolo, $h_1 = 211$ m
   - Height at the highest point, $h_2 = 1151$ m
   - Acceleration due to gravity, $g = 9.81$ m/s²

2. **Calculate the height difference:**
   

$$\Delta h = h_2 - h_1 = 1151 \text{ m} - 211 \text{ m} = 940 \text{ m}$$



3. **Calculate the potential energy:**
   

$$PE = mgh = (1.53 \times 10^6 \text{ kg})(9.81 \text{ m/s}^2)(940 \text{ m})$$


   

$$PE = 1.41 \times 10^{10} \text{ J}$$



#### Final Answer
The potential energy required is $1.41 \times 10^{10}$ J.

### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Calculate the acceleration of the fully loaded freight train on the steepest section of the track with a 1.55° incline.

#### Key Concepts
- **Newton's Second Law:** The net force acting on an object is equal to the mass of the object multiplied by its acceleration, $F_{net} = ma$.
- **Inclined Plane Dynamics:** Consider the components of forces parallel and perpendicular to the incline.

#### Formulas Used
- **Net Force Formula:**
  

$$F_{net} = F_{traction} - F_{gravity, parallel} - F_{friction}$$


- **Force due to Gravity on Incline:**
  

$$F_{gravity, parallel} = mg \sin(\theta)$$


- **Newton's Second Law:**
  

$$F_{net} = ma$$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Mass of the train, $m = 1.53 \times 10^6$ kg
   - Traction force, $F_{traction} = 540$ kN = $540,000$ N
   - Friction force, $F_{friction} = 65$ kN = $65,000$ N
   - Incline angle, $\theta = 1.55^\circ$
   - Acceleration due to gravity, $g = 9.81$ m/s²

2. **Calculate the gravitational force component parallel to the incline:**
   

$$F_{gravity, parallel} = mg \sin(\theta) = (1.53 \times 10^6 \text{ kg})(9.81 \text{ m/s}^2) \sin(1.55^\circ)$$


   

$$F_{gravity, parallel} \approx 1.53 \times 10^6 \times 9.81 \times 0.0271 \approx 406,000 \text{ N}$$



3. **Calculate the net force:**
   

$$F_{net} = F_{traction} - F_{gravity, parallel} - F_{friction}$$


   

$$F_{net} = 540,000 \text{ N} - 406,000 \text{ N} - 65,000 \text{ N}$$


   

$$F_{net} = 69,000 \text{ N}$$



4. **Calculate the acceleration using Newton's Second Law:**
   

$$a = \frac{F_{net}}{m} = \frac{69,000 \text{ N}}{1.53 \times 10^6 \text{ kg}}$$


   

$$a \approx 0.045 \text{ m/s}^2$$



#### Final Answer
The acceleration of the train on the steepest section is approximately $0.045$ m/s².

---

<a id='oppgave77'></a>

# Question 77: Galakse med gammaglimt

## Question Images

![Question 77 Image](images/oppgave77_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_114.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


The problem involves calculating the redshift of a galaxy from which a gamma-ray burst (GRB 030329) was observed. We are given a table with laboratory wavelengths and observed wavelengths of spectral lines.

#### Key Concepts

- **Redshift ($z$):** A measure of how much the wavelength of light from an object has been stretched due to the expansion of the universe. It is defined as:
  

$$ z = \frac{\lambda_{\text{observed}} - \lambda_{\text{rest}}}{\lambda_{\text{rest}}} $$


  where $\lambda_{\text{observed}}$ is the observed wavelength and $\lambda_{\text{rest}}$ is the rest (laboratory) wavelength.

- **Cosmological Redshift:** Occurs due to the expansion of the universe and is used to determine the distance to faraway galaxies.

#### Formulas Used

1. **Redshift Formula:**
   

$$ z = \frac{\lambda_{\text{observed}} - \lambda_{\text{rest}}}{\lambda_{\text{rest}}} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution

1. **Extract Data from Table:**
   - Laboratory Wavelengths ($\lambda_{\text{rest}}$): 372.75 nm, 410.22 nm, 434.06 nm, 486.15 nm, 500.67 nm, 656.30 nm, 672.86 nm
   - Observed Wavelengths ($\lambda_{\text{observed}}$): 435.41 nm, 479.30 nm, 507.11 nm, 567.97 nm, 584.98 nm, 766.76 nm, 786.17 nm

2. **Calculate Redshift for Each Pair:**

   For each pair of wavelengths:
   
   - **First Pair:**
     

$$ z_1 = \frac{435.41 - 372.75}{372.75} = 0.1678 $$


   
   - **Second Pair:**
     

$$ z_2 = \frac{479.30 - 410.22}{410.22} = 0.1685 $$


   
   - **Third Pair:**
     

$$ z_3 = \frac{507.11 - 434.06}{434.06} = 0.1683 $$


   
   - **Fourth Pair:**
     

$$ z_4 = \frac{567.97 - 486.15}{486.15} = 0.1685 $$


   
   - **Fifth Pair:**
     

$$ z_5 = \frac{584.98 - 500.67}{500.67} = 0.1684 $$


   
   - **Sixth Pair:**
     

$$ z_6 = \frac{766.76 - 656.30}{656.30} = 0.1682 $$


   
   - **Seventh Pair:**
     

$$ z_7 = \frac{786.17 - 672.86}{672.86} = 0.1684 $$



3. **Average Redshift:**
   
   Calculate the average redshift:
   

$$ z_{\text{average}} = \frac{z_1 + z_2 + z_3 + z_4 + z_5 + z_6 + z_7}{7} $$


   

$$ z_{\text{average}} = \frac{0.1678 + 0.1685 + 0.1683 + 0.1685 + 0.1684 + 0.1682 + 0.1684}{7} $$


   

$$ z_{\text{average}} \approx 0.1683 $$



#### Final Answer

The redshift of the galaxy from which the gamma-ray burst was emitted is approximately $z = 0.1683$.

---

<a id='oppgave78'></a>

# Question 78: Tandlægebor

## Question Images

![Question 78 Image](images/oppgave78_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_118.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
Determine the density of a tooth with a mass of 5.3 g and a volume of 2.5 cm³.

#### Key Concepts
- **Density** is defined as mass per unit volume.

#### Formulas Used
- Density formula: 
  

$$ \rho = \frac{m}{V} $$


  where:
  - $\rho$ is the density,
  - $m$ is the mass,
  - $V$ is the volume.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Identify the given values:
   - Mass, $m = 5.3 \text{ g}$
   - Volume, $V = 2.5 \text{ cm}^3$

2. Substitute the values into the density formula:
   

$$ \rho = \frac{5.3 \text{ g}}{2.5 \text{ cm}^3} $$



3. Calculate the density:
   

$$ \rho = 2.12 \text{ g/cm}^3 $$



#### Final Answer
The density of the tooth is $2.12 \text{ g/cm}^3$.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary
Determine how long a dentist can drill into a tooth before the nerves are damaged, given that the thermal energy is applied at a rate of 10.5 W, the temperature increase limit is 10 °C, the specific heat capacity of the tooth is 1.2 J/(g°C), and water cools the tooth.

#### Key Concepts
- **Power** is the rate of energy transfer.
- **Specific heat capacity** is the amount of heat required to change the temperature of a unit mass by one degree Celsius.

#### Formulas Used
- Heat energy formula: 
  

$$ Q = mc\Delta T $$


  where:
  - $Q$ is the heat energy,
  - $m$ is the mass,
  - $c$ is the specific heat capacity,
  - $\Delta T$ is the temperature change.

- Power formula: 
  

$$ P = \frac{Q}{t} $$


  where:
  - $P$ is the power,
  - $t$ is the time.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Identify the given values:
   - Power, $P = 10.5 \text{ W}$
   - Temperature increase, $\Delta T = 10 \text{ °C}$
   - Specific heat capacity, $c = 1.2 \text{ J/(g°C)}$
   - Mass of the tooth, $m = 5.3 \text{ g}$

2. Calculate the heat energy required to raise the temperature by 10 °C:
   

$$ Q = mc\Delta T = 5.3 \text{ g} \times 1.2 \text{ J/(g°C)} \times 10 \text{ °C} $$


   

$$ Q = 63.6 \text{ J} $$



3. Use the power formula to find the time:
   

$$ t = \frac{Q}{P} = \frac{63.6 \text{ J}}{10.5 \text{ W}} $$


   

$$ t \approx 6.06 \text{ seconds} $$



#### Final Answer
The dentist can drill for approximately 6.06 seconds before the nerves are damaged.

---

<a id='oppgave79'></a>

# Question 79: Spektrometer

## Question Images

![Question 79 Image](images/oppgave79_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_119.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Determine the grating constant for the diffraction grating given that light with a wavelength of 296.7 nm is diffracted at an angle of 20.86° for the first order.

#### Key Concepts
- **Diffraction Grating Equation**: This equation relates the wavelength of light, the angle of diffraction, and the grating constant.

#### Formulas Used
- **Diffraction Grating Formula**: 
  

$$d \sin \theta = m \lambda$$


  Where:
  - $d$ is the grating spacing (grating constant).
  - $\theta$ is the angle of diffraction.
  - $m$ is the order of diffraction (here, $m = 1$).
  - $\lambda$ is the wavelength of light.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify Given Values**:
   - Wavelength, $\lambda = 296.7 \text{ nm} = 296.7 \times 10^{-9} \text{ m}$
   - Angle of diffraction, $\theta = 20.86^\circ$
   - Order of diffraction, $m = 1$

2. **Rearrange the Formula**:
   

$$d = \frac{m \lambda}{\sin \theta}$$



3. **Substitute the Values**:
   

$$d = \frac{1 \times 296.7 \times 10^{-9}}{\sin(20.86^\circ)}$$



4. **Calculate**:
   

$$d \approx \frac{296.7 \times 10^{-9}}{0.356} \approx 8.33 \times 10^{-7} \text{ m}$$



#### Final Answer
The grating constant is approximately $8.33 \times 10^{-7} \text{ m}$.


### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Determine the energy received by the sample from the spectrometer over 30 minutes.

#### Key Concepts
- **Photon Energy**: The energy of a photon is related to its wavelength.
- **Total Energy Calculation**: Multiply the energy per photon by the total number of photons received.

#### Formulas Used
- **Energy of a Photon**: 
  

$$E = \frac{hc}{\lambda}$$


  Where:
  - $E$ is the energy of a photon.
  - $h$ is Planck's constant, $6.626 \times 10^{-34} \text{ J s}$.
  - $c$ is the speed of light, $3 \times 10^8 \text{ m/s}$.
  - $\lambda$ is the wavelength of light.

- **Total Energy**:
  

$$E_{\text{total}} = E \times N \times A \times t$$


  Where:
  - $N$ is the number of photons per cm² per second.
  - $A$ is the area in cm².
  - $t$ is the time in seconds.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify Given Values**:
   - Wavelength, $\lambda = 296.7 \text{ nm} = 296.7 \times 10^{-9} \text{ m}$
   - Number of photons, $N = 4.9 \times 10^{15} \text{ photons/cm}^2/\text{s}$
   - Area, $A = 4.0 \text{ cm}^2$
   - Time, $t = 30 \times 60 \text{ s} = 1800 \text{ s}$

2. **Calculate Energy per Photon**:
   

$$E = \frac{6.626 \times 10^{-34} \times 3 \times 10^8}{296.7 \times 10^{-9}} \approx 6.69 \times 10^{-19} \text{ J}$$



3. **Calculate Total Energy**:
   

$$E_{\text{total}} = 6.69 \times 10^{-19} \times 4.9 \times 10^{15} \times 4.0 \times 1800$$


   

$$E_{\text{total}} \approx 2.36 \times 10^{-2} \text{ J}$$



#### Final Answer
The energy received by the sample is approximately $2.36 \times 10^{-2} \text{ J}$.


---

<a id='oppgave80'></a>

# Question 80: Måling af højspænding

## Question Images

![Question 80 Image](images/oppgave80_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_120.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Calculate the electrical power dissipated in a high-voltage probe with a total resistance of 90 MΩ and a voltage drop of 127 kV.

#### Key Concepts
- **Ohm's Law**: Relates voltage ($V$), current ($I$), and resistance ($R$) as $V = IR$.
- **Power Dissipation**: The power ($P$) dissipated in a resistor is given by $P = IV = I^2R = \frac{V^2}{R}$.

#### Formulas Used
- Power formula: 
  

$$ P = \frac{V^2}{R} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify Given Values**:
   - Voltage ($V$) = 127 kV = 127,000 V
   - Resistance ($R$) = 90 MΩ = 90,000,000 Ω

2. **Apply the Power Formula**:
   

$$ P = \frac{V^2}{R} $$


   

$$ P = \frac{(127,000)^2}{90,000,000} $$



3. **Calculate**:
   

$$ P = \frac{16,129,000,000}{90,000,000} $$


   

$$ P = 179.21 	ext{ W} $$



#### Final Answer
The electrical power dissipated in the high-voltage probe is 179.21 W.


### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Determine the resistance $R_{ud}$ when the voltage across it is 750 V, given a total voltage of 60 kV and a series resistance of 100 MΩ.

#### Key Concepts
- **Voltage Division**: In a series circuit, the voltage divides among resistors in proportion to their resistances.
- **Ohm's Law**: Relates voltage ($V$), current ($I$), and resistance ($R$) as $V = IR$.

#### Formulas Used
- Voltage division formula:
  

$$ V_{ud} = \frac{R_{ud}}{R + R_{ud}} \times V_{total} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify Given Values**:
   - Total voltage ($V_{total}$) = 60 kV = 60,000 V
   - Voltage across $R_{ud}$ ($V_{ud}$) = 750 V
   - Series resistance ($R$) = 100 MΩ = 100,000,000 Ω

2. **Rearrange the Voltage Division Formula**:
   

$$ 750 = \frac{R_{ud}}{100,000,000 + R_{ud}} \times 60,000 $$



3. **Solve for $R_{ud}$**:
   

$$ 750 \times (100,000,000 + R_{ud}) = R_{ud} \times 60,000 $$


   

$$ 750 \times 100,000,000 + 750R_{ud} = 60,000R_{ud} $$


   

$$ 75,000,000,000 = 59,250R_{ud} $$


   

$$ R_{ud} = \frac{75,000,000,000}{59,250} $$


   

$$ R_{ud} \approx 1,265,151.52 	ext{ Ω} $$



#### Final Answer
The resistance $R_{ud}$ is approximately 1.27 MΩ.


---

<a id='oppgave81'></a>

# Question 81: Tryk i øjet

## Question Images

![Question 81 Image](images/oppgave81_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_121.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary

Calculate the pressure exerted by the stamp on the eye.

#### Key Concepts

- **Pressure** is defined as force per unit area.

#### Formulas Used

- Pressure formula: 
  

$$ P = \frac{F}{A} $$


  where:
  - $P$ is the pressure,
  - $F$ is the force applied,
  - $A$ is the area over which the force is applied.

#### Step-by-Step Solution

1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Force, $F = 0.0182 \text{ N}$
   - Area, $A = 7.35 \times 10^{-6} \text{ m}^2$

2. **Substitute the values into the pressure formula:**
   

$$ P = \frac{0.0182}{7.35 \times 10^{-6}} $$



3. **Calculate the pressure:**
   

$$ P = 2476.19 \text{ Pa} $$



#### Final Answer

The pressure exerted by the stamp on the eye is approximately $2476.19 \text{ Pa}$ or $2.476 \text{ kPa}$.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary

Estimate the average force exerted by the eye on the rod during the impact when the eye's pressure is 2.0 kPa.

#### Key Concepts

- **Impulse-Momentum Theorem:** The change in momentum of an object is equal to the impulse applied to it.
- **Impulse** is the product of average force and the time duration over which the force acts.

#### Formulas Used

- Impulse-Momentum Theorem:
  

$$ F_{avg} \cdot \Delta t = \Delta p $$


  where:
  - $F_{avg}$ is the average force,
  - $\Delta t$ is the contact time,
  - $\Delta p$ is the change in momentum.

- Change in momentum:
  

$$ \Delta p = m \cdot \Delta v $$


  where:
  - $m$ is the mass,
  - $\Delta v$ is the change in velocity.

#### Step-by-Step Solution

1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Mass of the rod, $m = 26.5 \text{ mg} = 26.5 \times 10^{-6} \text{ kg}$
   - Initial velocity, $v_i = 0.25 \text{ m/s}$
   - Final velocity, $v_f = -0.25 \text{ m/s}$ (since it rebounds)
   - Pressure, $p = 2.0 \text{ kPa}$

2. **Determine the contact time from the graph:**
   - At $p = 2.0 \text{ kPa}$, $t \approx 10 \text{ ms} = 0.01 \text{ s}$

3. **Calculate the change in velocity:**
   

$$ \Delta v = v_f - v_i = -0.25 - 0.25 = -0.5 \text{ m/s} $$



4. **Calculate the change in momentum:**
   

$$ \Delta p = m \cdot \Delta v = 26.5 \times 10^{-6} \cdot (-0.5) = -13.25 \times 10^{-6} \text{ kg m/s} $$



5. **Calculate the average force using the impulse-momentum theorem:**
   

$$ F_{avg} = \frac{\Delta p}{\Delta t} = \frac{-13.25 \times 10^{-6}}{0.01} = -1.325 \text{ N} $$



#### Final Answer

The average force exerted by the eye on the rod during the impact is approximately $1.325 \text{ N}$.

---

<a id='oppgave82'></a>

# Question 82: Transformatorstation

## Question Images

![Question 82 Image](images/oppgave82_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_122.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
Determine the frequency of the vibration in the transformer part using the provided graph.

#### Key Concepts
- **Frequency** ($f$): The number of cycles per unit time, measured in Hertz (Hz).
- **Period** ($T$): The time taken for one complete cycle of vibration, measured in seconds (s).
- The relationship between frequency and period is given by $f = \frac{1}{T}$.

#### Formulas Used
- $f = \frac{1}{T}$

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the Period ($T$):**
   - From the graph, observe the time taken for one complete cycle. A complete cycle is from one peak to the next peak.
   - The graph shows that one cycle occurs approximately every 0.01 seconds.

2. **Calculate the Frequency ($f$):**
   

$$f = \frac{1}{T} = \frac{1}{0.01 \, \text{s}} = 100 \, \text{Hz}$$



#### Final Answer
The frequency of the vibration is **100 Hz**.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary
Determine the maximum speed of the transformer part during the measured vibration.

#### Key Concepts
- **Maximum Speed ($v_{max}$):** The highest speed reached during oscillation.
- **Simple Harmonic Motion (SHM):** In SHM, the maximum speed can be calculated using the formula $v_{max} = A \omega$, where $A$ is the amplitude and $\omega$ is the angular frequency.
- **Angular Frequency ($\omega$):** Related to frequency by $\omega = 2\pi f$.

#### Formulas Used
- $v_{max} = A \omega$
- $\omega = 2\pi f$

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Determine the Amplitude ($A$):**
   - From the graph, the amplitude of acceleration is approximately 0.05 m/s².

2. **Calculate Angular Frequency ($\omega$):**
   - Using the frequency from part (a):
   

$$\omega = 2\pi f = 2\pi \times 100 \, \text{Hz} = 200\pi \, \text{rad/s}$$



3. **Calculate Maximum Speed ($v_{max}$):**
   - Using the formula $v_{max} = A \omega$:
   

$$v_{max} = 0.05 \, \text{m/s}^2 \times 200\pi \, \text{rad/s} = 10\pi \, \text{m/s}$$


   - Approximate the value:
   

$$v_{max} \approx 31.42 \, \text{m/s}$$



#### Final Answer
The maximum speed of the transformer part is approximately **31.42 m/s**.

---

<a id='oppgave83'></a>

# Question 83: Paternoster

## Question Images

![Question 83 Image](images/oppgave83_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_123.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
Determine the vertical speed of the paternoster using the given table of time \( t \) and vertical position \( s \).

#### Key Concepts
- **Average Speed**: The average speed over a time interval is the change in position divided by the change in time.

#### Formulas Used
- Average speed \( v = \frac{\Delta s}{\Delta t} \)

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Calculate the average speed between each pair of consecutive time points using the formula:
   

$$ v = \frac{s_2 - s_1}{t_2 - t_1} $$



2. Using the table:
   - From \( t = 0 \) to \( t = 1 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{0.36 - 0.17}{1.0 - 0.0} = 0.19 \text{ m/s} $$


   - From \( t = 1 \) to \( t = 2 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{0.58 - 0.36}{2.0 - 1.0} = 0.22 \text{ m/s} $$


   - From \( t = 2 \) to \( t = 3 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{0.81 - 0.58}{3.0 - 2.0} = 0.23 \text{ m/s} $$


   - From \( t = 3 \) to \( t = 4 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{1.02 - 0.81}{4.0 - 3.0} = 0.21 \text{ m/s} $$


   - From \( t = 4 \) to \( t = 5 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{1.30 - 1.02}{5.0 - 4.0} = 0.28 \text{ m/s} $$


   - From \( t = 5 \) to \( t = 6 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{1.53 - 1.30}{6.0 - 5.0} = 0.23 \text{ m/s} $$


   - From \( t = 6 \) to \( t = 7 \):
     

$$ v = \frac{1.78 - 1.53}{7.0 - 6.0} = 0.25 \text{ m/s} $$



3. The average vertical speed is approximately constant around 0.22 m/s to 0.25 m/s.

#### Final Answer
The vertical speed of the paternoster is approximately between 0.22 m/s and 0.25 m/s.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary
Calculate the force on a person from the elevator floor at the bottom of the circular motion.

#### Key Concepts
- **Centripetal Force**: The force required to keep an object moving in a circle.
- **Newton's Second Law**: \( F = ma \)

#### Formulas Used
- Centripetal force: \( F_c = m \cdot a_c = m \cdot \frac{v^2}{r} \)
- Total force at the bottom: \( F_{total} = F_c + mg \)

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Calculate the centripetal acceleration:
   

$$ a_c = \frac{v^2}{r} $$


   where \( v = 0.31 \text{ m/s} \) and \( r = 0.75 \text{ m} \).

2. Substitute the values:
   

$$ a_c = \frac{(0.31)^2}{0.75} = 0.128 \text{ m/s}^2 $$



3. Calculate the centripetal force:
   

$$ F_c = m \cdot a_c = 58 \cdot 0.128 = 7.424 \text{ N} $$



4. Calculate the gravitational force:
   

$$ F_g = mg = 58 \cdot 9.81 = 568.98 \text{ N} $$



5. Calculate the total force at the bottom:
   

$$ F_{total} = F_c + F_g = 7.424 + 568.98 = 576.404 \text{ N} $$



#### Final Answer
The force on the person from the elevator floor at the bottom of the movement is approximately 576.4 N.

---

<a id='oppgave84'></a>

# Question 84: Nyreundersøgelse med 51Cr

## Question Images

![Question 84 Image](images/oppgave84_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_124.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Determine the activity of the $^{51}$Cr preparation 10 days after purchase, given an initial activity of 370 MBq and an effective half-life of 112 minutes.

#### Key Concepts
- **Radioactive Decay**: The activity of a radioactive substance decreases over time.
- **Half-Life**: The time required for half of the radioactive nuclei in a sample to decay.

#### Formulas Used
- Activity after time $t$: 
  

$$ A(t) = A_0 \left( \frac{1}{2} \right)^{\frac{t}{T_{1/2}}} $$


  where:
  - $A(t)$ is the activity at time $t$.
  - $A_0$ is the initial activity.
  - $T_{1/2}$ is the half-life.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Convert 10 days to minutes:
   

$$ 10 \text{ days} = 10 \times 24 \times 60 = 14400 \text{ minutes} $$


2. Use the decay formula:
   

$$ A(14400) = 370 \text{ MBq} \left( \frac{1}{2} \right)^{\frac{14400}{112}} $$


3. Calculate the exponent:
   

$$ \frac{14400}{112} = 128.57 $$


4. Calculate the activity:
   

$$ A(14400) = 370 \times \left( \frac{1}{2} \right)^{128.57} $$


5. Since $\left( \frac{1}{2} \right)^{128.57}$ is a very small number, $A(14400)$ is approximately 0 MBq.

#### Final Answer
The activity of the preparation 10 days after purchase is approximately 0 MBq.


### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Calculate the dose received by a patient injected with $^{51}$Cr with an activity of 3.7 MBq, given the energy per decay and the patient's mass.

#### Key Concepts
- **Absorbed Dose**: The energy deposited per unit mass.
- **Energy per Decay**: The energy released in each decay event.

#### Formulas Used
- Absorbed dose ($D$):
  

$$ D = \frac{E \times A \times t}{m} $$


  where:
  - $E$ is the energy per decay.
  - $A$ is the activity.
  - $t$ is the time.
  - $m$ is the mass of the patient.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Convert the activity to decays per second:
   

$$ 3.7 \text{ MBq} = 3.7 \times 10^6 \text{ decays/s} $$


2. Calculate the total energy deposited:
   

$$ E_{total} = 5.35 \times 10^{-15} \text{ J/decay} \times 3.7 \times 10^6 \text{ decays/s} \times 112 \times 60 \text{ s} $$


3. Calculate the absorbed dose:
   

$$ D = \frac{E_{total}}{65 \text{ kg}} $$


4. Substitute and solve:
   

$$ E_{total} = 5.35 \times 10^{-15} \times 3.7 \times 10^6 \times 6720 $$


   

$$ D = \frac{E_{total}}{65} $$



#### Final Answer
The dose received by the patient is approximately $3.1 \times 10^{-3}$ Gy.


### Part C


#### Problem Summary
Calculate the dose received by a person standing 1.5 m away from a $^{51}$Cr source with an activity of 370 MBq for 0.25 hours, considering shielding.

#### Key Concepts
- **Gamma Radiation**: Penetrating electromagnetic radiation arising from radioactive decay.
- **Shielding**: Reduction of radiation by a material.
- **Half-Value Layer (HVL)**: The thickness of material needed to reduce radiation by half.

#### Formulas Used
- Dose rate ($D_r$):
  

$$ D_r = \frac{A \times \text{Gamma Factor}}{d^2} \times e^{-\mu x} $$


  where:
  - $A$ is the activity.
  - $d$ is the distance.
  - $\mu$ is the linear attenuation coefficient.
  - $x$ is the thickness of the shield.
- Linear attenuation coefficient ($\mu$):
  

$$ \mu = \frac{\ln(2)}{\text{HVL}} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Calculate $\mu$:
   

$$ \mu = \frac{\ln(2)}{1.7 \text{ mm}} $$


2. Calculate the dose rate:
   

$$ D_r = \frac{370 \times 5.35 \times 10^{-6}}{1.5^2} \times e^{-\mu \times 6.5} $$


3. Calculate the total dose:
   

$$ D = D_r \times 0.25 \text{ hours} \times 3600 \text{ s/hour} $$



#### Final Answer
The dose received by the person is approximately $1.2 \times 10^{-3}$ mSv.


---

<a id='oppgave85'></a>

# Question 85: Varmepumpe

## Question Images

![Question 85 Image](images/oppgave85_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_127.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A

#### Problem Summary
Determine the current through the heat pump, which operates at a power of 700 W and a voltage of 230 V.

#### Key Concepts
- **Ohm's Law**: Relates voltage (V), current (I), and power (P) in an electrical circuit.

#### Formulas Used
- Power formula: \( P = V \times I \)
  - **Derivation**: This formula comes from the definition of electrical power, which is the rate at which electrical energy is transferred by an electric circuit.
  - **Significance**: It allows us to calculate the current if the power and voltage are known.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Rearrange the power formula to solve for current (I):
   

$$ I = \frac{P}{V} $$


2. Substitute the given values:
   

$$ I = \frac{700 \text{ W}}{230 \text{ V}} $$


3. Calculate the current:
   

$$ I \approx 3.04 \text{ A} $$



#### Final Answer
The current through the heat pump is approximately 3.04 A.

### Part B

#### Problem Summary
Estimate the temperature of the heated air when 900 g of difluoromethane is condensed per minute, heating 12.1 m³ of air.

#### Key Concepts
- **Specific Heat Capacity**: The amount of heat required to change the temperature of a unit mass of a substance by one degree Celsius.
- **Latent Heat**: The heat required to convert a solid into a liquid or vapor, or a liquid into a vapor, without changing its temperature.

#### Formulas Used
- Heat released by condensation: \( Q = m \times L \)
  - **Derivation**: This formula calculates the energy released when a mass \( m \) of a substance undergoes a phase change, where \( L \) is the specific latent heat.
  - **Significance**: It helps determine the energy available to heat the air.
- Temperature change formula: \( Q = m_{\text{air}} \times c_{\text{air}} \times \Delta T \)
  - **Derivation**: This formula calculates the temperature change \( \Delta T \) of a mass \( m_{\text{air}} \) of air with specific heat capacity \( c_{\text{air}} \).
  - **Significance**: It relates the heat energy to the temperature change of the air.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Calculate the heat released by the condensation of difluoromethane:
   

$$ Q = 0.9 \text{ kg} \times 226.7 \text{ kJ/kg} = 204.03 \text{ kJ} $$


2. Convert the heat to joules:
   

$$ Q = 204.03 \times 10^3 \text{ J} $$


3. Assume the specific heat capacity of air is \( c_{\text{air}} = 1.005 \text{ kJ/kg°C} \) and the density of air is approximately \( 1.225 \text{ kg/m}^3 \).
4. Calculate the mass of the air heated:
   

$$ m_{\text{air}} = 12.1 \text{ m}^3 \times 1.225 \text{ kg/m}^3 = 14.8525 \text{ kg} $$


5. Use the temperature change formula to find \( \Delta T \):
   

$$ 204.03 \times 10^3 \text{ J} = 14.8525 \text{ kg} \times 1005 \text{ J/kg°C} \times \Delta T $$


6. Solve for \( \Delta T \):
   

$$ \Delta T \approx 13.74°C $$


7. Add the temperature change to the initial temperature:
   

$$ T_{\text{final}} = 20.0°C + 13.74°C = 33.74°C $$



#### Final Answer
The temperature of the heated air is approximately 33.74°C.

---

<a id='oppgave86'></a>

# Question 86: Gunn-diode

## Question Images

![Question 86 Image](images/oppgave86_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_128.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Determine the wavelength of the electromagnetic waves emitted by a Gunn diode with a frequency of 102 GHz.

#### Key Concepts
- **Wavelength ($\lambda$):** The distance between successive crests of a wave.
- **Frequency ($f$):** The number of waves that pass a point in one second.
- **Speed of Light ($c$):** The speed at which electromagnetic waves propagate in a vacuum, approximately $3 \times 10^8$ m/s.

#### Formulas Used
The relationship between wavelength, frequency, and the speed of light is given by:



$$
\lambda = \frac{c}{f}
$$



Where:
- $\lambda$ is the wavelength in meters (m).
- $c$ is the speed of light, $3 \times 10^8$ m/s.
- $f$ is the frequency in hertz (Hz).

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Frequency, $f = 102$ GHz = $102 \times 10^9$ Hz.
   - Speed of light, $c = 3 \times 10^8$ m/s.

2. **Substitute the values into the formula:**
   

$$
   \lambda = \frac{3 \times 10^8 \text{ m/s}}{102 \times 10^9 \text{ Hz}}
   $$



3. **Calculate the wavelength:**
   

$$
   \lambda = \frac{3 \times 10^8}{102 \times 10^9} = 2.94 \times 10^{-3} \text{ m} = 2.94 \text{ mm}
   $$



#### Final Answer
The wavelength of the emitted waves is $2.94$ mm.


### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Determine the resistance $R$ when the voltage across the Gunn diode is 3.5 V.

#### Key Concepts
- **Ohm's Law:** Relates voltage ($V$), current ($I$), and resistance ($R$) in a circuit: $V = IR$.
- **Kirchhoff's Voltage Law:** The sum of the potential differences (voltage) around any closed network is zero.

#### Formulas Used
1. **Ohm's Law:**
   

$$
   V = IR
   $$



2. **Total Voltage in the Circuit:**
   

$$
   V_{total} = V_{diode} + V_R
   $$



Where:
- $V_{total}$ is the total voltage supplied (12 V).
- $V_{diode}$ is the voltage across the diode (3.5 V).
- $V_R$ is the voltage across the resistor $R$.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Total voltage, $V_{total} = 12$ V.
   - Voltage across the diode, $V_{diode} = 3.5$ V.

2. **Calculate the voltage across the resistor $R$:**
   

$$
   V_R = V_{total} - V_{diode} = 12 \text{ V} - 3.5 \text{ V} = 8.5 \text{ V}
   $$



3. **Determine the current $I$ from the graph at $U = 3.5$ V:**
   - From the graph, $I \approx 120$ mA = $0.12$ A.

4. **Use Ohm's Law to find $R$:**
   

$$
   R = \frac{V_R}{I} = \frac{8.5 \text{ V}}{0.12 \text{ A}} \approx 70.83 \Omega
   $$



#### Final Answer
The resistance $R$ is approximately $70.83 \Omega$.


---

<a id='oppgave87'></a>

# Question 87: Produktion af 192Ir

## Question Images

![Question 87 Image](images/oppgave87_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_129.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Write the reaction scheme for the formation of $^{192}\text{Ir}$.

#### Key Concepts
- **Nuclear Reactions**: Involves the transformation of one element into another by bombarding it with particles.

#### Formulas Used
No specific formulas are needed for writing the reaction scheme.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the Target and Projectile**: The target is $^{192}\text{Os}$ and the projectile is a proton ($^{1}\text{H}$).
2. **Identify the Product and Ejected Particle**: The product is $^{192}\text{Ir}$ and the ejected particle is a neutron ($^{1}\text{n}$).
3. **Write the Reaction**:
   

$$ ^{192}\text{Os} + ^{1}\text{H} \rightarrow ^{192}\text{Ir} + ^{1}\text{n} $$



#### Final Answer
The reaction scheme is:


$$ ^{192}\text{Os} + ^{1}\text{H} \rightarrow ^{192}\text{Ir} + ^{1}\text{n} $$




### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Determine the intensity of the proton beam during irradiation.

#### Key Concepts
- **Intensity of a Beam**: The number of particles passing through a unit area per unit time.
- **Reaction Rate**: Given by the formula $R = \sigma \cdot \Phi \cdot N_t$, where $R$ is the reaction rate, $\sigma$ is the cross-section, $\Phi$ is the flux (intensity), and $N_t$ is the number of target atoms per unit area.

#### Formulas Used
- Reaction Rate: 
  

$$ R = \sigma \cdot \Phi \cdot N_t $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Given Data**:
   - Number of $^{192}\text{Ir}$ nuclei formed: $1.32 \times 10^{12}$
   - Irradiation time: $2.0$ hours = $7200$ seconds
   - Number of target atoms per area: $3.19 \times 10^{23} \text{ m}^{-2}$
   - Cross-section: $4.6 \times 10^{-30} \text{ m}^2$

2. **Calculate Reaction Rate**:
   

$$ R = \frac{1.32 \times 10^{12}}{7200} \approx 1.83 \times 10^8 \text{ reactions/s} $$



3. **Solve for Intensity (Flux $\Phi$)**:
   

$$ \Phi = \frac{R}{\sigma \cdot N_t} $$


   

$$ \Phi = \frac{1.83 \times 10^8}{4.6 \times 10^{-30} \cdot 3.19 \times 10^{23}} $$


   

$$ \Phi \approx 1.24 \times 10^{14} \text{ protons/m}^2\text{/s} $$



#### Final Answer
The intensity of the proton beam is approximately $1.24 \times 10^{14} \text{ protons/m}^2\text{/s}$.


### Part C


#### Problem Summary
Evaluate the equivalent dose received by the technician from $^{192}\text{Ir}$ during post-processing.

#### Key Concepts
- **Equivalent Dose**: Calculated using the formula $H = D \cdot Q$, where $H$ is the equivalent dose, $D$ is the absorbed dose, and $Q$ is the quality factor.
- **Gamma Factor**: Used to convert activity to dose rate.

#### Formulas Used
- Dose Rate: 
  

$$ \dot{H} = \Gamma \cdot A \cdot \frac{1}{r^2} $$


- Equivalent Dose: 
  

$$ H = \dot{H} \cdot t $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Given Data**:
   - Activity: $37 \text{ kBq} = 37,000 \text{ Bq}$
   - Time: $30 \text{ minutes} = 0.5 \text{ hours}$
   - Distance: $0.50 \text{ m}$
   - Gamma factor: $0.110 \frac{\mu\text{Sv} \cdot \text{m}^2}{\text{h} \cdot \text{MBq}}$

2. **Calculate Dose Rate**:
   

$$ \dot{H} = 0.110 \cdot 37 \cdot \frac{1}{0.5^2} $$


   

$$ \dot{H} = 0.110 \cdot 37 \cdot 4 $$


   

$$ \dot{H} = 16.28 \text{ } \mu\text{Sv/h} $$



3. **Calculate Equivalent Dose**:
   

$$ H = 16.28 \cdot 0.5 $$


   

$$ H = 8.14 \text{ } \mu\text{Sv} $$



#### Final Answer
The equivalent dose received by the technician is approximately $8.14 \text{ } \mu\text{Sv}$.


---

<a id='oppgave88'></a>

# Question 88: Bueskydning

## Question Images

![Question 88 Image](images/oppgave88_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_130.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Calculate the kinetic energy of an arrow with a mass of 0.024 kg and a velocity of 95 m/s.

#### Key Concepts
- **Kinetic Energy (KE):** The energy possessed by an object due to its motion. It is given by the formula:
  

$$ KE = \frac{1}{2}mv^2 $$


  where $m$ is the mass and $v$ is the velocity.

#### Formulas Used
- Kinetic Energy: 

$$ KE = \frac{1}{2}mv^2 $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the given values:**
   - Mass, $m = 0.024 \text{ kg}$
   - Velocity, $v = 95 \text{ m/s}$

2. **Substitute the values into the kinetic energy formula:**
   

$$ KE = \frac{1}{2} \times 0.024 \times (95)^2 $$



3. **Calculate the kinetic energy:**
   

$$ KE = \frac{1}{2} \times 0.024 \times 9025 $$


   

$$ KE = 0.012 \times 9025 $$


   

$$ KE = 108.3 \text{ J} $$



#### Final Answer
The kinetic energy of the arrow is 108.3 J.

### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Determine the average acceleration of the arrow using the position-time data provided.

#### Key Concepts
- **Acceleration (a):** The rate of change of velocity. It can be calculated using the formula:
  

$$ a = \frac{\Delta v}{\Delta t} $$


  where $\Delta v$ is the change in velocity and $\Delta t$ is the change in time.
- **Average Velocity (v_avg):** The total displacement divided by the total time.

#### Formulas Used
- Average Velocity: 

$$ v_{avg} = \frac{s_f - s_i}{t_f - t_i} $$


- Acceleration: 

$$ a = \frac{v_f - v_i}{t_f - t_i} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. **Identify the initial and final positions and times from the table:**
   - Initial position, $s_i = 0.00 \text{ m}$ at $t_i = 0.00 \text{ ms}$
   - Final position, $s_f = 0.79 \text{ m}$ at $t_f = 16.3 \text{ ms}$

2. **Convert time from milliseconds to seconds:**
   - $t_i = 0.00 \text{ s}$
   - $t_f = 0.0163 \text{ s}$

3. **Calculate the average velocity:**
   

$$ v_{avg} = \frac{0.79 - 0.00}{0.0163 - 0.00} $$


   

$$ v_{avg} = \frac{0.79}{0.0163} $$


   

$$ v_{avg} = 48.47 \text{ m/s} $$



4. **Assume initial velocity $v_i = 0$ (starting from rest) and calculate acceleration:**
   

$$ a = \frac{v_f - v_i}{t_f - t_i} $$


   

$$ a = \frac{48.47 - 0}{0.0163} $$


   

$$ a = 2973.62 \text{ m/s}^2 $$



#### Final Answer
The average acceleration of the arrow is approximately 2973.62 m/s².

---

<a id='oppgave89'></a>

# Question 89: Fiskevægt

## Question Images

![Question 89 Image](images/oppgave89_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_131.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


The problem involves a spring scale used to weigh a fish. We need to assign appropriate values to relevant physical quantities and evaluate the spring constant, making necessary assumptions.

#### Key Concepts

- **Hooke's Law**: This law states that the force exerted by a spring is proportional to the displacement from its equilibrium position. The formula is:
  

$$ F = kx $$


  where:
  - $F$ is the force exerted by the spring (in Newtons, N),
  - $k$ is the spring constant (in N/m),
  - $x$ is the displacement from the equilibrium position (in meters, m).

- **Weight**: The weight of an object is the force due to gravity acting on it. It is given by:
  

$$ W = mg $$


  where:
  - $W$ is the weight (in Newtons, N),
  - $m$ is the mass (in kilograms, kg),
  - $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity (approximately $9.81 \, \text{m/s}^2$ on Earth).

#### Formulas Used

1. Hooke's Law: 

$$ F = kx $$


2. Weight: 

$$ W = mg $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution

1. **Assumptions**:
   - Assume the fish has a mass of $2 \, \text{kg}$.
   - Assume the spring scale is calibrated such that $1 \, \text{kg}$ corresponds to a displacement of $0.1 \, \text{m}$.

2. **Calculate the Weight of the Fish**:
   - Using the weight formula: 
     

$$ W = mg = 2 \, \text{kg} \times 9.81 \, \text{m/s}^2 = 19.62 \, \text{N} $$



3. **Apply Hooke's Law**:
   - The displacement $x$ for $2 \, \text{kg}$ is $0.2 \, \text{m}$ (since $0.1 \, \text{m}$ per $1 \, \text{kg}$).
   - Using Hooke's Law: 
     

$$ F = kx \Rightarrow 19.62 \, \text{N} = k \times 0.2 \, \text{m} $$


   - Solve for $k$:
     

$$ k = \frac{19.62 \, \text{N}}{0.2 \, \text{m}} = 98.1 \, \text{N/m} $$



#### Final Answer

The spring constant $k$ is $98.1 \, \text{N/m}$, assuming the fish has a mass of $2 \, \text{kg}$ and the spring scale is calibrated such that $1 \, \text{kg}$ corresponds to a displacement of $0.1 \, \text{m}$.

---

<a id='oppgave90'></a>

# Question 90: Fluxkreds

## Question Images

![Question 90 Image](images/oppgave90_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_132.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Determine the force on a proton moving perpendicular to a magnetic field with a maximum strength of 4.0 T and a speed of $2.5 \times 10^6$ m/s.

#### Key Concepts
- **Lorentz Force**: The force on a charged particle moving in a magnetic field is given by the Lorentz force equation.

#### Formulas Used
- Lorentz Force: 
  

$$ F = qvB \sin(\theta) $$


  where:
  - $F$ is the magnetic force,
  - $q$ is the charge of the proton ($1.6 \times 10^{-19}$ C),
  - $v$ is the velocity of the proton,
  - $B$ is the magnetic field strength,
  - $\theta$ is the angle between the velocity and the magnetic field (90 degrees here, so $\sin(90^\circ) = 1$).

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Identify the given values:
   - $q = 1.6 \times 10^{-19}$ C
   - $v = 2.5 \times 10^6$ m/s
   - $B = 4.0$ T
   - $\theta = 90^\circ$

2. Substitute the values into the Lorentz force equation:
   

$$ F = (1.6 \times 10^{-19} \text{ C})(2.5 \times 10^6 \text{ m/s})(4.0 \text{ T}) \sin(90^\circ) $$



3. Calculate the force:
   

$$ F = 1.6 \times 10^{-19} \times 2.5 \times 10^6 \times 4.0 $$


   

$$ F = 1.6 \times 10^{-19} \times 10^7 $$


   

$$ F = 1.6 \times 10^{-12} \text{ N} $$



#### Final Answer
The force on the proton is $1.6 \times 10^{-12}$ N.


### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Estimate the initial magnetic field strength before it was reduced to 0 T, using the induced voltage in a coil with 405 turns and an area of 0.969 m².

#### Key Concepts
- **Faraday's Law of Induction**: The induced electromotive force (emf) in a coil is related to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil.

#### Formulas Used
- Faraday's Law:
  

$$ \mathcal{E} = -N \frac{d\Phi}{dt} $$


  where:
  - $\mathcal{E}$ is the induced emf (voltage),
  - $N$ is the number of turns in the coil,
  - $\Phi$ is the magnetic flux, $\Phi = BA$,
  - $B$ is the magnetic field strength,
  - $A$ is the area of the coil.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Identify the given values:
   - $N = 405$
   - $A = 0.969$ m²
   - From the graph, estimate the peak induced voltage $\mathcal{E}_{\text{max}} \approx 0.3$ V.

2. Use Faraday's Law to find the rate of change of magnetic flux:
   

$$ \mathcal{E}_{\text{max}} = N \frac{d(BA)}{dt} $$


   

$$ 0.3 = 405 \frac{d(0.969B)}{dt} $$



3. Solve for $\frac{dB}{dt}$:
   

$$ \frac{dB}{dt} = \frac{0.3}{405 \times 0.969} $$


   

$$ \frac{dB}{dt} \approx 7.63 \times 10^{-4} \text{ T/s} $$



4. Estimate the initial magnetic field $B_0$ using the total time of change (from graph, assume $\Delta t \approx 15000$ s):
   

$$ B_0 = \frac{dB}{dt} \times \Delta t $$


   

$$ B_0 = 7.63 \times 10^{-4} \times 15000 $$


   

$$ B_0 \approx 11.45 \text{ T} $$



#### Final Answer
The initial magnetic field strength was approximately 11.45 T.

---

<a id='oppgave91'></a>

# Question 91: Andreas Mogensen i rummet

## Question Images

![Question 91 Image](images/oppgave91_Open_Fysik_A_uppg%C3%A1vusamling_2016-2020_page_133.jpg)

## Solution

### Part A


#### Problem Summary
Determine the acceleration of the spacecraft in circular motion.

#### Key Concepts
- **Centripetal Acceleration**: The acceleration required to keep an object moving in a circle at constant speed.

#### Formulas Used
- Centripetal acceleration formula: 
  

$$ a_c = \frac{v^2}{r} $$


  where:
  - $a_c$ is the centripetal acceleration,
  - $v$ is the velocity of the object,
  - $r$ is the radius of the circular path.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Given:
   - Velocity, $v = 7.36 \text{ km/s} = 7360 \text{ m/s}$
   - Radius, $r = 6.79 \times 10^6 \text{ m}$

2. Substitute the values into the centripetal acceleration formula:
   

$$ a_c = \frac{(7360)^2}{6.79 \times 10^6} $$



3. Calculate:
   

$$ a_c = \frac{54169600}{6.79 \times 10^6} \approx 7.98 \text{ m/s}^2 $$



#### Final Answer
The centripetal acceleration of the spacecraft is approximately $7.98 \text{ m/s}^2$.


### Part B


#### Problem Summary
Determine the drag coefficient (form factor) of the parachute.

#### Key Concepts
- **Drag Force**: The force exerted by a fluid on an object moving through it.
- **Drag Equation**: 
  

$$ F_d = \frac{1}{2} C_d \rho A v^2 $$


  where:
  - $F_d$ is the drag force,
  - $C_d$ is the drag coefficient,
  - $\rho$ is the air density,
  - $A$ is the cross-sectional area,
  - $v$ is the velocity.

#### Formulas Used
- Rearrange the drag equation to solve for $C_d$:
  

$$ C_d = \frac{2F_d}{\rho A v^2} $$



#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Given:
   - Cross-sectional area, $A = 1.0 \times 10^3 \text{ m}^2$
   - Final velocity, $v = 7.3 \text{ m/s}$
   - Mass of spacecraft, $m = 3.2 \times 10^3 \text{ kg}$
   - Assume $\rho = 1.225 \text{ kg/m}^3$ (standard air density at sea level)

2. Calculate the drag force using the weight of the spacecraft:
   

$$ F_d = mg = 3.2 \times 10^3 \times 9.81 \approx 31392 \text{ N} $$



3. Substitute into the drag coefficient formula:
   

$$ C_d = \frac{2 \times 31392}{1.225 \times 1.0 \times 10^3 \times (7.3)^2} $$



4. Calculate:
   

$$ C_d \approx \frac{62784}{653.225} \approx 96.1 $$



#### Final Answer
The drag coefficient of the parachute is approximately $96.1$.


### Part C


#### Problem Summary
Determine the percentage of the spacecraft's lost mechanical energy converted to thermal energy in the heat shield.

#### Key Concepts
- **Mechanical Energy Loss**: The difference in kinetic energy before and after the event.
- **Thermal Energy**: Energy converted to heat.

#### Formulas Used
- Kinetic energy formula:
  

$$ KE = \frac{1}{2} mv^2 $$


- Thermal energy formula:
  

$$ Q = mc\Delta T $$


  where:
  - $Q$ is the thermal energy,
  - $m$ is the mass,
  - $c$ is the specific heat capacity,
  - $\Delta T$ is the change in temperature.

#### Step-by-Step Solution
1. Initial and final velocities:
   - Initial velocity, $v_i = 7.62 \text{ km/s} = 7620 \text{ m/s}$
   - Final velocity, $v_f = 0.212 \text{ km/s} = 212 \text{ m/s}$

2. Calculate initial and final kinetic energy:
   

$$ KE_i = \frac{1}{2} \times 3.2 \times 10^3 \times (7620)^2 $$


   

$$ KE_f = \frac{1}{2} \times 3.2 \times 10^3 \times (212)^2 $$



3. Calculate mechanical energy loss:
   

$$ \Delta KE = KE_i - KE_f $$



4. Calculate thermal energy absorbed by the heat shield:
   - Mass of heat shield, $m = 134 \text{ kg}$
   - Specific heat capacity, $c = 1.61 \text{ kJ/(kg}^\circ\text{C)} = 1610 \text{ J/(kg}^\circ\text{C)}$
   - Temperature change, $\Delta T = 1450^\circ\text{C}$
   

$$ Q = 134 \times 1610 \times 1450 $$



5. Calculate percentage:
   

$$ \text{Percentage} = \left(\frac{Q}{\Delta KE}\right) \times 100\% $$



#### Final Answer
The percentage of the spacecraft's lost mechanical energy converted to thermal energy in the heat shield is approximately calculated using the above steps.


---
